Objective 5.1.5: List the effects of cyberbullying and strategies in preventing it. 
 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
 
Negative Effects of 
Cyberbullying  
 
There are many detrimental 
outcomes associated with 
cyberbullying that reach 
into the real world. Many 
targets report feeling: 
 
 
Depressed 
 
Sad 
 
Angry 
 
Frustrated 
 
Low Self esteem 
 
Anxiety 
 
Family problems 
 
Academic 
difficulties 
 
School violence 
 
Suicidal 
thoughts/attempts 
 
Cyberbullying Prevention 
 
 
Educate yourself on 
what cyberbullying 
is 
 
Protect your 
password 
 
Keep photos PG 
 
Pause before you 
post 
 
Raise awareness 
 
Set up privacy 
controls 
 
Never open 
messages from 
people you don’t 
know 
 
Log out of accounts 
on public 
computers

Search, Unscramble)

Objective 5.2.1a: Describe a computer and state types of digital computers 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
  
A computer is an electronic 
device that manipulates 
information, or data. 
  
Computers come in many 
shapes and sizes, and they 
perform many different 
functions in our daily lives.  
  
Computers exist in many 
digital devices that we use 
on a day-to-day basis. 
  
When you withdraw cash 
from an ATM, scan groceries 
at the store, or use a 
calculator, you're using a 
type of computer. 
  
Desktop Computers 
Computers designed to be 
placed on a desk and used in 
that spot. They need a 
constant supply of 
electricity to function. 
  
Laptop Computers 
Battery-powered all-in-one 
computers that are more 
portable than desktops, 
allowing you to use them 
almost anywhere. 
  
Tablet Computers 
Handheld computers that 
are even more portable than 
laptops. 
  
Embedded Computers 
Many of today's electronics 
are basically specialized 
computers, though we don't 
  
Think-Pair-Share: Have 
students share with a 
partner their thoughts on 
what makes a device a 
computer. 
  
  
Have students watch the 
‘What is a Computer’ video. 
  
 
 
Have students complete a 
compare and contrast 
worksheet on the types of 
computers. 
 
  
  
  
 
 
Have students complete an 
interactive on identifying 
embedded computers. 
 
  
 
Have students read/listen to 
the book ‘Goodnight iPad’ 
and list the digital devices 
mentioned. 
 
 
 
  
Write the Room 
Paste numbered 
descriptions and images of 
the types of personal 
computers around the 
room. Have students walk 
around and write the 
number along with the 
matching name on a paper 
or in their book. This can 
also be done in reverse. 
Have students write a 
description for a posted 
name or picture. 
 
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
Journal Writing/Blogging 
In at least three sentences, 
describe a computer in your 
own words. 
  
  
Have students create a 
slideshow/video showcasing 
types of computers and a 
few examples.

Objective 5.2.1b: Identify digital devices and their parts 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
  
The basic parts of a desktop 
computer are the system 
unit, monitor, keyboard, 
and mouse. 
  
Laptop computers have all 
their parts in one case – 
screen, keyboard, and 
touchpad. 
  
Instead of a keyboard and 
mouse, tablet computers 
use a touch-sensitive screen 
for typing and navigation.1 
  
While some of their external 
parts may be different, they 
all have similar internal 
components.  
  
Some internal components 
of a computer are: 
- central processing unit 
(CPU) 
- mother board  
- RAM 
- hard drive 
- power supply 
- video card 
 
- sound card8 
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
Have students watch the 
‘Basic Parts of a Computer’ 
video. 
  
  
  
Have students complete the 
‘Computer Parts Hangman’ 
game. 
  
Complete the ‘Find the 
Technology’ interactive 
search. [Whole 
Class/Group/Individual] 
  
  
  
  
  
 
 
 
Have students watch the 
‘Inside a Computer’ video. 
  
  
 
Have students read/listen to 
the book ‘Little Red Hen 
Builds a Computer’ and list 
the internal components 
mentioned. Then, research 
to discover the function of 
the parts. 
 
 
Have students complete the 
‘Build your own Computer’ 
activity. 
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
 
 
 
Have students complete a 
worksheet labeling the parts 
of digital devices. 
[Print/Digital]

Objective 5.2.2: Define and classify hardware components 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
  
A computer is made up of 
many parts that work 
together. 
  
The parts of the computer 
that can be seen and 
touched are called 
hardware.2 
  
Each hardware component 
has a specific job it does to 
help the digital device work. 
  
Five groups that hardware 
components can be divided 
into are: 
  
- Input Devices – used to 
enter data into the 
computer. Data can be 
letters, numbers, sounds, or 
images. Examples: mouse, 
keyboard, stylus, smart 
pencil, touchscreen, joystick, 
remote control, touchpad, 
scanner, digital camera, web 
camera, microphone, 
drawing tablet, and 
interactive whiteboard. 
  
 
 
 
 
- Output Devices – used to 
hear and see information 
from the computer. You use 
an output device to see or 
hear information from the 
computer. Information can 
be sound through speakers, 
  
Have students watch the 
video ‘Computer Devices’. 
Clarify for students that a 
CPU is a chip found inside of 
the system unit/tower. 
  
Have students complete a 
Quizizz identifying 
hardware components for 
each group. 
[Individual]

Have students share with a 
partner their definition of 
hardware and provide 
examples. 
  
  
 
Have students complete a 
sorting worksheet with a 
collection of hardware 
components. [Print/Digital] 
 
  
Have students create a 
crossword puzzle that 
contains the names and 
clues for 5 input devices, 5 
output devices, 5 storage 
devices. They may also 
include devices that can 
have two functions.

Objective 5.2.3: Construct a representation of an IPO cycle 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
  
A computer helps us 
generate information from 
raw data.  
  
It follows the Input-
Process-Output (IPO) cycle: 
  
- We use an input device to 
enter data into a computer. 
This data is called the input. 
  
- The CPU converts the data 
into meaningful 
information. This is called 
processing.  
  
- During the processing, the 
data or information are 
stored in the computer’s 
memory 
  
- After the data is processed, 
the result is conveyed 
through an output device. 
This is the output.5 
  
Have students watch the 
‘How Does a Computer 
Work?’ video. 
  
  
Have students complete a 
Quizizz identifying the 
input, process, and output 
of various IPO cycles. 
[Whole Class/ Group/ 
Partner/Individual] 
  
  
Present students with a 
variety of IPO cycles and 
have them identify the 
activity at each stage. [Print 
or Digital Worksheet 
/Notebook] 
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
Have students create a 
PowerPoint to display a 
representation of an IPO 
cycle. 
  
How Does a Computer Work 
video: 
https://youtu.be/3e0aN_pPh
ME 
  
IPO Cycle Quizizz: 
https://quizizz.com/admin/q
uiz/60ee7229fa248c001e16c
0ad

Objective 5.2.4: Explain the purpose of software 
  
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
  
Software are instructions 
that tell the computer what 
to do. There are two main 
types: system software and 
application software. 
  
System Software are the 
programs that run behind 
the scenes to ensure the 
computer functions 
properly, like the operating 
system and utility programs. 
  
An operating system is the 
most important software 
that runs on a computer. It 
manages the computer's 
memory and processes, as 
well as all its software and 
hardware. Without an 
operating system, a 
computer is useless.9 
  
Application Software are 
the programs used to 
perform specific computer 
tasks. 
  
They can be divided into 
two groups – general 
purpose and special 
purpose. 
  
 
General Purpose software to 
carry out lots of different 
tasks using that application. 
  
 
Special Purpose software 
perform one specific task 
  
Round Robin Question – 
What is software? 
  
Share with students the 
‘What is Software’ video. 
  
Share with students the 
‘Understanding Operating 
Systems’ video. 
  
Scavenger Hunt 
Use your Internet sleuthing 
skills to match the name of 
the operating system to its 
logo. 
  
 
 
 
 
Have students perform a 
digital research scavenger 
hunt to find examples of 
application software based 
on their uses. 
  
  
 
Using a T-Chart, have 
students sort general-
purpose and special- 
purpose software. 
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
Have students create a short 
video (Flipgrid) explaining 
the purpose of the different 
types of software. 
  
  
  
  
What is Software Video: 
https://youtu.be/PBDlbSAd
dAI 
  
Understanding Operating 
Systems video: 
https://youtu.be/fkGCLIQx1
MI

Software: 
https://technostacks.com/bl
og/types-of-application-
software

https://info.flipgrid.com/

The word ‘app’ is short for

Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
  
Modern operating systems 
use a graphical user 
interface, or GUI 
(pronounced gooey). A GUI 
lets you use your mouse to 
click icons, buttons, and 
menus, and everything is 
clearly displayed on the 
screen using a combination 
of graphics and text.9

and battery. [Whole Class]

together all the time.

symbols.

pictures that tell you 
something, like which 
bathroom to use, where to 
throw your trash, or when

They are easily understood 
by people around the world. 
  
When you use technology, 
you will see even more 
symbols.6

Objective 5.2.6a: Evaluate cloud computing. 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
  
The cloud (cloud computing 
or cloud storage) is the 
Internet - more specifically, 
it's all the things you can 
access remotely over the 
Internet. When something is 
in the cloud, it means it's 
stored on Internet servers 
instead of your computer's 
hard drive. 
  
Two main reasons people 
use the cloud are 
convenience and reliability. 
They can store files, share 
files, back up data for future 
use.7 
  
  
  
Have students watch the 
‘What is a Cloud?’ video. 
  
  
  
  
  
Have students create a 
poster on cloud computing. 
  
Have students research and 
debate the pros and cons of 
cloud computing.

Objective 5.5.1: Define coding and programming 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
  
Coding is writing commands 
to tell the computer to do 
something in a 
programming language it 
can understand. 
  
To start coding, you have to 
know a programming 
language, but you also have 
to understand how a 
computer thinks so that you 
can give it the right kinds of 
instructions. 
  
Code is a special language 
that a computer 
understands. An algorithm 
written in code is called a 
program.20 
  
Examples of Coding 
Languages  
  
- Scratch: a visual coding 
system that uses colored 
blocks and premade graphics 
to create games and apps.  
  
- Lego Mindstorms NXT: a 
language used by the FIRST 
Robotics League  
  
- Python: a general-purpose 
language that can be used 
for different tasks  
  
- HTML/CSS: These are 
markup languages and not 
programming languages. A 
markup language is a way to 
design and present text.  
  
During Teaching 
Have students watch the 
‘What is computer 
programming’ video. 
  
  
Blindfold one student and 
have the class direct them 
around the room.13 [Whole 
Class] 
  
  
Have students write 
instructions on how to get 
to a mystery location 
around the school using 
such instructions as “Go 
forward x steps”, “turn left”, 
and “turn right”.15 
[Group/Partner] 
  
  
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
Have students create a 
poster or infographic 
explaining coding and 
programming. 
  
 
 
 
 
Have students create a mind 
map highlighting different 
programming languages. 
  
  
  
BrainPop: What is computer 
programming: 
https://youtu.be/pKBw98uH
Oyk

programming: 
https://www.bbc.co.uk/bites
ize/guides/zts8d2p/revision/

Objective 5.5.2: Describe computational thinking. 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
  
Computational thinking 
means planning, problem-
solving, and analyzing 
information the way a 
computer does.17 
  
The cornerstones of 
computational thinking are 
decomposition, pattern 
making, abstraction, and 
algorithms. 
  
  
Vocabulary 
1. decomposition: 
break a problem 
down into smaller 
pieces 
2. pattern making: 
finding similarities 
between things 
3. abstraction: pulling 
out specific 
differences to make 
one solution work 
for multiple 
problems 
4. algorithm: a list of 
steps that you can 
follow to finish a 
task13 
  
Each cornerstone is as 
important as the others. 
They are like legs on a table 
- if one leg is missing, the 
table will probably collapse. 
Correctly applying all four 
techniques will help when 
programming a computer.16 
  
  
Have students journal their 
thoughts on computational 
thinking and its importance. 
[Individual] 
  
  
Have students view the 
‘Computational Thinking for 
Children’ video. Discuss the 
terms explained in the 
video. [Whole Class/Partner] 
  
  
Tut, Clap, or Jive 
Show students a sequence 
of hand movements (hand 
jive, tutting, or clapping). 
Make sure the sequence is 
relatively complex or long so 
that it is not easily 
remembered without 
breaking it down.  
  
Model how to break down 
the sequence into smaller 
parts. Show how to number 
and/or name each part and 
draw an image of each part. 
  
Show another video of hand 
movements and have 
students decompose the 
sequence on a paper.14 
[Individual/Partner] 
  
  
Have students create an 
infographic that will explain 
computational thinking to 
the class. 
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
Computational Thinking for 
Children Video: 
https://www.youtube.com/
watch?v=mUXo-S7gzds  
  
  
 
Decomposition unplugged 
activity KS2. 
https://www.barefootcomp
uting.org/resources/decomp
osition-unplugged-activity-
ks2 
  
  
Tutting Video: 
https://www.youtube.com/
watch?v=axpDFvUz8Eo 
  
Hand Jive Video: 
https://www.youtube.com/
watch?v=eIozjNOgrm8 
  
Clapping Video (00:58): 
https://www.youtube.com/
watch?v=ibr1OVTZNIU

Objective 5.5.3: Define and identify algorithms 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
  
An algorithm lists the steps 
needed to complete a task. 
Computer scientists use 
algorithms to plan out the 
steps they want a computer 
to follow.  
  
Programs are created to 
implement algorithms. 
  
Algorithms can be 
represented as pseudocode 
or a flowchart, and 
programming is the 
translation of these into a 
computer program.  
  
If an algorithm has been 
designed, the computer 
program will follow this 
algorithm, step-by-step, 
which will tell the computer 
exactly what it should do. 
  
Examples of algorithms in 
everyday life are: recipes, 
traffic lights, GPS, brushing 
your teeth, and planting a 
seed. 
  
  
  
Round Robin: What are 
algorithms? 
 
Have students view the 
‘Algorithms’ video. What are 
some of the algorithms they 
see in the day-to-day living? 
[Whole Class Discussion]  
  
Write the steps for folding a 
paper airplane on the board 
out of order. Have the 
students unjumble the steps 
and then create a paper 
airplane. 
  
Have students complete 
page 3 in the Act 2 
workbook by drawing a line 
from each step in the 
Algorithm to the matching 
code block. 
  
Have students identify the 
algorithms for getting to 
class from the front of the 
school. [Partner/Group] 
  
Have students develop an 
algorithm to solve an 
assigned problem using a 
specific set of commands 
and use peer review to 
critique the solution. 
[Peer Evaluation] 
  
  
GCF – Algorithms: 
https://edu.gcfglobal.org/en
/computer-
science/algorithms/1/ 
  
  
Computer Science Basics – 
Algorithms Video: 
https://www.youtube.com/
watch?v=sHyA_Q9dz0I

Workbook:

Objective 5.5.4: Demonstrate knowledge of the Scratch interface 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
  
Scratch is an environment 
where you can build 
algorithms by combining 
code blocks together. 
  
You can create interactive 
stories, animations, 
artwork, and games. 
  
There are three main 
sections of the Scratch 
interface. 
  
On the left-hand side we 
have tools to control or 
change our characters. The 
main way is through our 
code blocks.  
  
There are different types of 
block categories or ways to 
control our characters.  
  
We can also change the way 
our characters look under 
the “costumes” tab. 
  
We can also add sound 
under the “sounds” tab. 
  
 
 
In the middle we have our 
scripts area. This is where 
we put together code blocks 
to create our algorithms, or 
instructions, for our 
character.  
  
We “drag and drop” the code 
blocks we want to use.  
  
  
Have students view the 
‘Scratch Basics’ video. 
Discuss products that can be 
made in Scratch, and the 
method used. 
  
 
Open a New Project (click 
on “create” on the top left) 
and explain the different 
components of the Scratch 
Interface. Have students 
view the Exploring Scratch 
3.0 sheet of the student 
workbook as a reference. 
[Individual] 
  
 
 
 
 
 
 Pair and Share: Have 
students share with a 
partner what they would like 
to create in Scratch. Have a 
few students share their 
thoughts with the class. 
[Partner] 
  
  
Have students log into their 
accounts and explore the 
interface. Introduce the 
menu options: My Stuff; My 
Class; Studio. [Individual] 
  
  
Have students access the 
Hello Mr. Scratch project 
and use the blocks available. 
[Individual/Partner] 
  
Have students complete a 
LiveWorksheet, Kahoot, or 
Quizizz identifying the parts 
of the Scratch interface. 
  
Pinnguaq Scratch Basics 
Video: 
https://www.youtube.com/
watch?v=NqMd44Oi2l4

Objective 5.5.5a: Use sequences in an algorithm 
 
 
 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
  
Sequence is a set of 
instructions that follow one 
another in order.  
  
Understanding that 
computers use sequence to 
follow instructions will help 
you as you code. 
  
An example of a sequence is 
instructions to brush your 
teeth.  
  
  
Have students watch the 
‘What is a Sequence’ video. 
[0:00 – 2:23]

steps for brushing their 
teeth. Encourage them to 
use transition or ordinal 
words first, next, then, last 
or first, second, third, etc. 
while putting the steps in 
order. [Whole Class]

everyday tasks (eating 
breakfast, getting dressed, 
getting to school, etc.). 
Then write down the 
sequence of instructions in 
their workbook for 
completing one of these 
tasks.

Objective 5.5.5b: Identify events 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
  
An Event is an action that 
causes something to 
happen. 
  
Think of the comprehension 
strategy of Cause and 
Effect. The Cause is the 
Action (Event) the Effect is 
the action(s) that Happen(s). 
  
Events occur in many places 
in your life: pressing the play 
button on a video, knocking 
on a door, tapping someone 
on the shoulder…  
  
A script in Scratch always 
begins with an event block 
(sometimes called an event 
hat).20 
  
  
  
Have students view the 
‘Events’ video. 
  
  
  
Complete the ‘Big Event’ 
activity from the Teachers 
Guide. [Whole Class]

students to brainstorm 
other events and share an 
example with a partner. 
Then have persons to share 
with the class.

workbook.

Objective 5.5.5c: Demonstrate loops and animation 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
  
A loop is a sequence of 
instructions that is 
repeated. 
  
The repeat loop block in 
Scratch looks like a 
sandwich. All of the blocks 
inside the loop (sandwich) 
are run in order (sequence) 
and  
  
repeated the number of 
times listed in the repeat 
oval. 
  
  
Inquiry Prompt 
What kinds of things can 
you program Sprites to do 
using loops?  [moving, 
jumping, changing color, etc]  
  
  
Just like in real life, in order 
for these actions to occur in 
a computer program, 
animation is needed to 
show them happening. 
  
Animation cycles through a 
sequence of images of the 
characters that look slightly 
different. As you move 
quickly through the pictures, 
it looks like the character is 
moving. 
  
Animation in programming 
works the same way that we 
think of animation in real 
life.  
  
  
Introduce the concept of 
loops with the ‘Loopy 
Dance’ activity. 
  
  
Have students think about 
things they do in a loop. 
Discuss. Examples: blinking, 
breathing, heart beating, 
jumping jacks, walking. 
  
  
 
 
 
Journal Writing/Blogging: 
What are some examples of 
animation? (Possible 
responses: cartoons, flip 
books, animated movies)

Video

workbook or have them 
design their own. Discuss 
how they would animate the

Objective 5.3.1: Define the term keyboarding and label the parts of the keyboard 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
   
Keyboarding is the process 
of inputting text (type) into 
a keyboard by pressing keys 
on a keyboard.  A keyboard 
is an input device.  
 
A keyboard has letter keys, 
number keys and special 
keys.  The letters, numbers 
and symbols are called 
characters.  
 
You type letters, numbers 
and symbols to create 
documents. 
 
You use a keyboard to work 
on the Internet, play some 
games, and when you use 
most software.  
 
The most commonly used 
keyboard is the “Qwerty”.  
It is named after the top row 
of letters on the keyboard.  
It was invented in 1864 by 
Christopher Latham Sholes. 
 
 
   
Watch videos of different 
shapes and types of 
keyboards. 
 
Explain the parts of the 
keyboards on different 
devices. 
 
Label the keyboard and 
explain their various parts 
   
Label the keyboard. 
  
Explain the various parts of 
the keyboard. 
 
Matching the keys with their 
functions.

keyboard worksheet:

.com/zl2394360jb

Worksheet: 
https://www.liveworksheets
.com/oj2322222mb

Techniques Slide Show:

Objective 5.3.2: Demonstrate proper keyboarding posture 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
   
How you sit when you use a 
keyboard is important.  How 
you sit is called posture.  
Good posture is important 
because not sitting correctly 
can result in injuries to your 
body.  
 
You should sit up straight 
when you use the keyboard.  
You should face the 
computer screen.  Your 
arms should rest in front of 
you.  Your hands should be 
clean.  You should place 
your fingers gently on the 
keys.  
 
When typing your work area 
should be arranged as 
follows:  
 
Keyboard directly 
in front of chair; 
front edge of 
keyboard even with 
edge of desk  
 
Monitor placed for 
easy viewing  
 
Book at right of 
keyboard  
 
Show video to demonstrate 
proper/correct posture. 
 
Explain the importance of 
having good posture. 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
   
 
 
 
 
 
 
Differentiation    
Identify good and bad 
posture from pictures using 
yes and no responses.  
 
Collaboration  
Create short videos to 
demonstrate the Do’s and 
Don’ts of proper posture.   
 
   
Proper Keyboarding 
Techniques: 
https://www.youtube.com/
watch?v=ee9eIsUzEOM

Objective 5.3.3: Demonstrate correct finger placement and reach techniques  
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
 
Finger Placement 
When you use a keyboard:    
Curve your fingers 
upright over the 
home keys,   
 
Keep your wrists 
low but not 
touching the 
keyboard,   
 
Hold your forearms 
parallel to the slant 
of the keyboard,   
 
Keep your body 
erect, sitting back 
in the chair   
 
Keep your feet flat 
on the floor  
 
The keys on the middle row 
of the keyboard are called 
the home row keys.    
 
The home keys are 
a s d f for the left 
hand and j k l ; for 
the right hand  
 
 
 
When you are 
ready to keyboard, 
you rest your 
fingertips on the 
home row keys.  
 
When you type a 
character that is 
 
Show video to demonstrate 
correct finger placement. 
  
Observe students placing 
fingers correctly on home 
row keys. 
 
Students will practice typing 
the characters from the 
home row keys without 
looking at the keyboard 
 
Students may use printed 
keyboard replicas to 
practice home row finger 
placing and practice. 
 
Teacher may call characters 
from the home row keys as 
student type. 
 
Provide reinforcement 
exercises. 
  
Touch type home row keys 
lessons. 
 
Touch type simple words 
and sentences from the 
home row.

Objective 5.3.4: Identify and use special keys 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
   
Backspace - Deletes a 
character to the left of the 
cursor 
 
Caps Lock – Capitalizes all 
letters. 
 
Delete – Deletes a character 
to the right of the cursor. 
 
Enter – Completes or enters 
a command.  Moves cursor 
down to the next line. 
 
Shift Keys – Capitalizes 
letters.  Inserts symbols.  
Press and hold the Shift key, 
then press another key to 
capitalize a letter or to insert 
a symbol. 
 
Tab – Indents 
 
Esc - Short for Escape, Esc is 
a key found on the top-left 
corner of a computer 
keyboard. It allows the user 
to abort, cancel, or close an 
operation. 
   
The spacebar - the longest 
bar at the bottom of the 
keyboard.  
 
The Backspace Key - helps 
you to erase a mistake on 
your screen, just like you 
would use an eraser in your 
book.  
 
   
Watch appropriate video of 
special keys. 
 
 Have students explain the 
functions of the special keys 
and features on the 
different devices. 
 
Provide reinforcement 
activities. 
   
Identify the special keys on 
the keyboard  
 
Match the keys with their 
functions. 
 
Type lists of simple words 
using the special keys. 
 
Classwork 
 
Quiz

watch?v=geKIJEghaqU 
 
Special Keys 
https://www.youtube.com/
watch?v=4XS1_j1XhCE

Bahamas Ministry of Education Primary Computer Studies Curriculum Guide

Go to Table of Contents 
Content

Suggested Assessment(s)

The Directional or Arrow 
Keys - help you to move the 
cursor up, down, left and 
right without erasing any of 
your work.  
 
Shift Keys - The keyboard 
has 2 shift keys. Hold down 
the shift key on the left side 
when you want to type 
capital letters with your 
right hand. Hold down the 
shift key on the right side 
when you want to type 
capital letters with your left 
hand. You hold down the 
shift key then press a letter 
key to type a capital letter. 
 
Lower case letters are small 
letters (such as a, e, or t).  
These letters will be 
obtained by pressing the 
assigned key.  
   
Upper case are capital 
letters (such as A, E, or T). 
They are obtained by using 
the caps lock key or the shift 
keys.  To do this, hold down 
the shift key while pressing 
the letter to make it 
capitalized or press the Caps 
lock key which would also 
allow letters to also be 
typed in uppercase.  
  
When new keys are 
introduced, you are required 
to take your time in order to 
get used to the position of 
the keys.   
 
The movement to and from 
each key should be quick 
and a part of the act of

Content

Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
striking.  
 
Return your fingers to the 
home keys immediately 
after striking the new keys.

Objective 5.3.7a: Identify features and ribbon tabs of the Word interface.   
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
  
Some of the features of MS 
Word are as follows: 
 
Title Bar:  This contains the 
name of the document and 
the name of the program, as 
well as the minimize, 
maximize/restore down and 
close icons. 
 
Quick Access Toolbar:  
frequently used commands 
are placed in the quick 
access toolbar. 
 
Ribbon:  this allows you to 
quickly locate the 
commands that you need in 
order to complete a task. 
 
Ribbon Tabs:  a ribbon tab 
contains a series of related 
icons grouped together to 
access commands. 
 
Scroll Bars:  moves the 
page up and down or left to 
right. 
 
Minimize:  hides the 
window from the screen and 
places it in the taskbar. 
 
Maximize/Restore Down:  
expands the window to full 
screen/decrease the size of 
the window to only full part 
of the screen. 
 
Close:  closes the window. 
 
   
Open MS Word and explain 
the key features of a typical 
window. 
 
 
 
 
 
Explain Tabs on the Ribbon. 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
   
Label the diagram of a MS 
Word window. 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
Explain the features of the 
MS Word window.

features, shortcuts, uses, 
and other related questions

m/faqs/what-is-ms-word-
and-its-
features/articleshow/84464
446.cms

Objective 5.3.7b: Enter and format text. 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
  
The Work Area 
 
After the Word window 
opens, there is a blank space 
for you to begin typing, 
similar to when you begin to 
write on a blank sheet of 
paper.  There is a blinking 
black line on the screen 
called the cursor.  This 
cursor indicates where the 
next character will be typed. 
 
Saving a Document 
 
It is very important to save 
your document in the event 
that you may wish to edit it 
or use it at a later date. 
 
Save your document as soon 
as you begin typing, and 
then save the changes about 
every five minutes as you 
type so you don’t lose your 
work. 
 
 
 
 
 
Step 1: Start a new 
document in Word and type 
your text. 
 
Step 2: Click File in the top 
left-hand corner of the 
screen. 
 
Step 3: From the menu, 
choose Save. 
 
   
Teacher would demonstrate 
the use of the following:  
 
add text 
 
enter text 
 
format text: font, 
style, size, and 
color 
 
adjust line spacing 
 
insert and format 
WordArt 
 
insert and format 
clip art or picture 
file 
 
modify the text 
wrap of an object 
 
draw and format 
shapes 
 
scale, move, and 
rotate objects 
 
insert a simple 
page border 
 
spell check a 
document 
 
print preview 
 
 
print a document 
 
cut, copy, and 
paste a selection 
 
copy formatting 
from a selection 
 
Use spell check 
features in simple 
documents. 
 
Name, save, open, and print 
simple documents. 
 
 
 
 
 
 
Create and format simple 
text documents using font, 
style, color, bold, italic, 
underline, alignment, select, 
cut, copy, and paste 
options.

Step 4: A ‘Save’ dialogue 
box will come up. At the top

be shown at the very top of 
your document screen. If 
you make changes to your 
document and then save 
them after it have been 
saved originally, the 
dialogue box will not come 
up again. It will just save 
your changes without any 
visual notification being 
shown.

Objective 5.4.1: Define graphics and multimedia 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
 
GRAPHICS 
 
Graphics are all around us.  
Our world is made up of 
colors, shapes and words.  
Graphics are drawings and 
pictures. 
 
Examples of graphics may 
be found on: 
 
 product wrappers 
and packaging 
 Story books and 
textbook covers 
 t-shirts 
 School bags 
 Face painting 
Graphic designs creatively 
put together colors, shapes, 
and words to form 
meaningful and pleasing 
design. 
  
 
 
 
 
MULTIMEDIA 
 
Multi means more than one; 
many or multiple. 
 
Media is a means of 
conveying information. 
 
Multimedia is the 
presentation of information 
through text, audio, 
graphics, video, and 
  
Identify and discuss the 
different types of graphics in 
surroundings and personal 
items 
 
Describe graphic designs 
created

designers

animation.  
 
The basic elements of 
multimedia are:  
 
 Text – Characters 
that are used to 
create word, 
sentence and 
paragraphs. 
 
 Graphics – are 
digital 
representation of 
non-text 
information such as 
drawings, charts, or 
photographs. 
 
 Audio – Music, 
speech or any other 
sound. 
 
 Video – photograph 
images that are 
played back at 
speeds of 15 – 30 
frames per second 
and provide that 
appearance of full 
motion 
 
 Animation – 
Clipping through a 
series of still images 
that create an 
illusion of motion.

Objective 5.4.2: Explain the use of presentation software 
  
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
   
A presentation lets you 
combine text, graphics, 
video, and sound on 
individual pages which are 
called slides.  Many slides 
are saved into one file.  This 
is called a presentation.  
Presentations are called 
slide shows. 
 
Presentation software 
enables users to present 
information, graphics, 
videos, etc. through 
slideshows in an attractive 
way. 
 
Popular Presentation 
software include  Prezi, 
Google Slides, Keynote, 
Slides, Slide Dog, Canva, 
and PowerPoint. 
   
Watch video introducing 
popular presentation 
software

compare and contrast 
popular presentation 
software.  Examples:  Prezi, 
Google Slides, Keynote, 
Slides, Slide Dog, and 
PowerPoint

Objective 5.4.3: Explain PowerPoint 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
 
PowerPoint is one of many 
software designed for 
making electronic slides/ 
presentations. 
 
The PowerPoint application 
lets you combine text, 
graphics, video, and sound 
on individual pages which 
are called slides. This file is 
called a presentation.        
 
A new blank presentation 
opens each time you start 
PowerPoint. 
 
You can use many devices 
to help make and give a 
presentation.  
Presentations are also called 
slide shows 
 
NOTE:  The PowerPoint 
window, and the screen 
resolution may look 
different based on the 
device used. 
  
Other 
Multimedia/Presentation 
Programs include:   
Google Slides                   
Slidebean                  
Powtoon 
Prezi                                  
Emaze 
Canva                                
SlideShare 
 
  
Explain the Backstage View 
and the template themes 
 
Demonstrate proper design 
guidelines to use 
PowerPoint to create, save 
and view slides. 
 
Explain the different slide 
layouts 
 
Research and use another 
Presentation software to 
present a slideshow. 
  
Produce a 3 slides 
presentation with text, 
pictures about an event. 
 Format text using 
different fonts and 
colors for 
enhancements 
 Add transition to 
the slide 
 Display the slides 
using the slideshow 
feature 
  
PowerPoint Software

PowerPoint

Objective 5.4.4: Identify the features of the PowerPoint interface 
  
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
 
The PowerPoint window has 
many of the same elements 
as other Microsoft 
programs.  It has the same 
toolbar buttons and menus 
used to open, save, draw 
objects, cut, copy, paste, 
insert clipart, check spelling, 
preview, print, etc. 
 
The PowerPoint window 
also has many new features 
that you use to create, 
format and view slides. 
 
Office button – displays a 
drop-down menu for 
creating, opening, saving, 
and printing 
 
Title Bar – displays the 
filename and program 
 
Ribbon – displays tabs that 
organize program 
commands by groups. 
 
Command buttons – are 
displayed beneath the tabs.  
They are used to execute a 
command or to display a 
drop-down menu of 
command options 
 
 
Outline tab – used to create 
and view slides in an outline 
format, 
 
Slides tab – used to see a 
tiny version of each slide 
  
Demonstrate and explain 
the features of the MS 
PowerPoint window. 
 
Labeling diagrams 
 
Watch appropriate video 
 
 
  
 Label the features of the 
PowerPoint window 
diagram. 
 
Introducing the PowerPoint 
Window 
https://www.thetraininglady
.com/powerpoint-window/ 
 
Diagram of PowerPoint 
window.

dpress.com/2013/03/ppt_scr
een.png?w=300&h=210

ngpowerpoint/wp-

3/05/pptwindow2-
1024x664.png

that have been created, 
called a thumb nail. 
 
Slide pane – contains the 
current slide. 
 
Placeholders – are boxes 
with dotted boarders that 
are part of most slide 
layouts.  These boxes hold 
title and body text or 
objects such as charts, 
tables, and pictures   
Placeholders used to add 
text, drawings, clipart, video 
and sound to a slide. 
 
Note pane – is located below 
the slide pane and is used to 
type reference notes and 
additional comments about 
the slide. 
 
Drawing toolbar - 
Automatically displayed at 
the bottom of the window 
above the status bar. 
 
Status bar – shows the 
number of the slide in the 
slide pane and the total 
number of slides in the 
presentation.

Objective 5.4.5: Name the various slide layouts 
  
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
  
Slide Layouts are the pre-
formatted design of a slide 
in PowerPoint.  
 
These are:  
 
 Title slide – first 
and main slide, 
to introduce the 
topic and 
presenter. 
 Title and content 
slide  
 Two Content 
 Comparison 
 Title Only 
When you create a slide, you 
choose a layout.  The way 
objects are put on a slide is 
the layout. 
 
You need to decide on the 
layout of each new slide you 
insert  
  
 Explain the use of each 
layout 
  
  
 
Different Types of Slide 
Layouts in PowerPoint 
https://www.pokeslide.com/
en/different-types-of-slide-
layout-in-powerpoint/

Objective 5.4.6: Create a title slide and format text 
  
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
 
Whenever you create a new 
slide, you’ll need to choose a 
slide layout. 
 
Slide layouts contain place 
holders.  Place holders are 
pre-made boxes on a slide 
that allow you to enter 
information into a slide by 
clicking. 
 
The title slide is the first 
slide of a presentation.  It 
usually contains a title and a 
subtitle. 
 
The title tells the main idea 
of the presentation.     
 
To create a title page: 
 
1. Open PowerPoint. 
You are presented 
with a title slide. 
 
2. Enter the 
Presentation title in 
the ‘Click to Add 
Title’ text 
box/placeholder.  
 
3. Type your subtitle 
in the Click to Add 
Subtitle text 
box/placeholder. 
   
   
Students will watch a video 
demonstrating how to 
create and format a title 
slide. 
 
Teacher will lead students in 
Creating a title slide 
inserting text and graphics. 
 
 
 
   
Create a PowerPoint 
presentation 
 
 
 
Generate content for a 5-
slide presentation

Objective 5.4.7: Insert and format new slides adding texts and graphics 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
 
To create a new slide: 
 
1. Choose the Home 
tab. 
2. Click the New Slide 
button 
 in 
the Slides group. 
The Office Theme 
dialog box appears 
and displays several 
layout templates. 
 
3. Click the layout you 
want. The layout 
appears in the Slide 
pane of the 
PowerPoint 
window. 
To add text 
 
1. To add text, click 
inside the 
placeholder and 
type. 
 
To add an additional slide to 
your presentation, do one of 
the following: 
 
1. Right-click the slide 
layout. A menu 
appears. Click 
Layout and then 
click the layout you 
want. 
2. Choose the Home 
tab, click the New 
Slide button

Objective 5.4.8: Add animation to text and graphics 
  
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
   
To add an animation effect 
to a PowerPoint slide, follow 
the steps below. 
 
1. In a slide, highlight 
the text or image 
you want to 
animate. 
 
2. On the Ribbon click 
the Animations tab. 
 
3. On the Animations 
tab, in the 
Advanced 
Animation section, 
click the Add 
Animation option. 
 
4. Select the desired 
type of animation 
effect.  
 
You can select an Entrance, 
Emphasis, and Exit 
animation effect.  
 
You can also select a Motion 
Path effect, if you want to 
change the motion path of 
the animation. 
   
   
   
   
  
Adding Animation: 
https://www.computerhope.
com/issues/pictures/powerp
oint-add-animation.jpg

Objective 5.4.9: Preview, save, print, and deliver a presentation. 
  
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
   
Navigating the Slide Show 
 
If you want to go to the next 
slide do one of the 
following: 
     Press the Right Arrow 
key. 
     Press the Enter key. 
     Press the Page Down key. 
     Left click the slide. 
  
If you want to go to the 
previous slide do one of the 
following: 
     Press the Left Arrow key. 
     Press the Backspace key. 
     Press the Page Up key. 
 
To end the slide show and 
return to PowerPoint press 
the Esc key.

Objective 5.6.1: Explain the use of the Excel program 
 
 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
 
Microsoft Excel (or Excel) is 
a program used to record, 
analyze, present reports 
that need calculations, such 
as a grade sheet, and to 
create charts. 
 
A spreadsheet is a table of 
rectangular grid, consisting 
of cells (rows and columns), 
that holds the data, which 
includes texts and numbers. 
 
Spreadsheets are used in 
business for budgeting, 
financial reporting, etc. 
Spreadsheet can be used for 
personal budgeting, 
tracking expenses, or 
creating a list of personal 
items. 
    
The advantage of an 
electronic spreadsheet is 
that the content can be 
easily edited and updated to 
reflect changes in the 
calculated data. 
 
Project-Based Learning 
Activity 
 
PowerPoint presentations 
 
Appropriate 
presentation/videos 
 
Sample Personal Budget 
Spreadsheet 
 
Sample Fast-Food-Fun 
Spreadsheet 
 
 
List personal items that are 
very important for life. 
 
Plan a Personal budget – 
identify needs, listing items, 
costs, and calculate total. 
 
Enter data from the 
Personal Budget list. Budget 
list to include the dollar 
signs and commas. 
 
Save the sketches to use in 
creating a new excel 
worksheet.

Objective 5.6.2: Demonstrate opening and closing a workbook and a worksheet 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
 
To start Excel:  
 
1) On the Windows 
taskbar, click the Start 
button to open the 
Start menu. 
2) On the Start menu, 
scroll through the list of 
apps, then click Excel. 
Excel will open in 
Backstage view. 
 
The Backstage view allows 
for the use of a blank 
workbook, open an existing 
workbook, or use a preset 
workbook called a template.  
 
The File tab on the Ribbon, 
shows various screens of 
commands that can be used 
to manage files and options 
in using Excel. 
 
TOUCH SCREEN DEVICES    
 
Point out the differences in 
the Office and windows 
interfaces. (Ribbon 
increases in height, buttons 
are bigger with more space 
around each, to move easily 
using the fingers or a stylus 
to tap the button.) 
 
Closing a Workbook  
 
1) On the ribbon, click the 
File tab to display the 
Backstage view, and 
then click Close in the 
navigation bar (or press

used to choose and

current cell with the 
thick rectangular border

An excel file is called a 
Workbook. A workbook 
contains one or more 
individual worksheets. 
 
Worksheet – contains grid, 
make up of rows and 
columns. 
 
Cell – A cell is the 
intersection of a row and a 
column. (Contain text, 
number or formula) Cell 
Range 
 
Label – Texts entry or data 
 
Values – Numeric values; 
default at right aligned 
 
Formulas – calculation 
commands that perform 
operations on the data. (Cell 
references, arithmetic

Objective 5.6.4: Navigate within a worksheet 
 
 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessments 
Resources 
 
Moving around the cells of a 
worksheet using the 
following methods:  
 
Pointing and clicking in a 
cell (block plus sign cursor) 
Scroll Bars arrows;  
 
Directional Arrows or 
Cursor Control Keys (Left, 
Right, Up, Down); Home 
Key and CTRL + Home, End, 
CTRL +G or F5 (Go To dialog 
box to move quickly to a cell 
address. TAB Key; PGUP, 
PGDN.  
 
The horizontal and vertical 
scroll bars to move to other 
areas of the worksheet. 
 
Project-Based Learning 
Activity 
 
Presentation videos 
 
 
 
Students should identify 
these keys on their device 
and practice moving around 
the worksheet

Review Questions 
 
Labeling a diagram, naming 
the keys.

Objective 5.6.5: Create a blank worksheet or use a template to enter data  
 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
 
Create a new workbook 
from the new screen in 
Backstage view. Use the 
blank workbook template or 
open an existing one. 
 
Note: using the CTRL + N or 
a new blank document in 
any Office application. 
 
To enter data into a cell, it 
must be selected. The 
easiest way to select a cell 
(make it active) is to use the 
mouse to move the block 
plus sign pointer to the cell 
and click it. Use the Arrow 
Keys. When the cell is 
selected, the thick border 
surrounds the cell, and the 
active cell reference appears 
in the Name Box. The active 
cell column and row 
headings color changes to a 
darker shade. 
Enter data into a cell and 
pressing the Enter key, 
moving the cell cursor to the 
next cell in the column. 
 
Project-Based Learning 
Activity 
 
Presentation Video 
 
Create a worksheet, and 
enter texts, numbers and 
dates.  
 
Explain the different data 
types and their 
position/alignment in a cell. 
 
Selecting a cell, range of 
cells and to point out the 
active cell.

Students to use their sample 
Personal Budget sketch 
spreadsheets and to enter 
the data in a new 
worksheet.

Students to work from other 
assigned tasks.

Objective 5.6.6: Format, save, and print a worksheet 
 
 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
 
Formatting enhances the 
appearance of the 
worksheet data by changing 
font, size, color, alignment, 
and adding borders. Borders 
are useful when a worksheet 
is printed, to show the 
gridlines 
 
Saving a worksheet – This is 
done to keep the document 
for later use or to share with 
others. Using the Backstage 
view – File – Save or Save 
As. From the Keyboard: Ctrl 
+S in all Office Program. 
 
Printing is necessary for a 
paper-based copy of the 
worksheet. From the File – 
Backstage View. Excel has 
many tools to control the 
print layout and appearance 
of a worksheet. Preview 
before printing for 
correctness. 
 
 
 
Project-Based Learning 
Activity 
 
Presentation Videos 
 
Sample formatted 
worksheet. 
 
Demonstrate the uses of the 
Save/Save As commands 
and print options.

worksheet.

save, preview, and print a 
hard copy or Screen Share  
 
Test/Quiz – Multiple choice, 
True/False, Matching, Fill-in 
the Blanks

Objective 5.6.7: Perform simple calculations using formulas and the SUM function 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
 
A formula is a calculation 
using numbers in a cell. 
Using a formula to calculate 
values allow you to focus on 
the data and allow Excel to 
automatically recalculate 
the results, if the data has to 
be changes. 
 
To begin a formula in any 
cell, it must begin with the 
equal (=) sign/symbol. Then 
a cell address, a 
mathematical operator, 
then another cell address. 
Example: = B2+C3 
 
Enter a cell address into a 
formula by typing it directly 
into the cell. By clicking on 
the cell to be included. The 
cell into which you enter a 
formula will display the 
result. 
  
Note: the formula will be 
seen in the formula Bar. 
 
Introduce Common Built-In 
Functions 
      
A function is pre-set 
operator in Excel to accept 
the values/numbers, and cell 
references when selected 
for calculations. 
 
Examples: =SUM to add the 
total of the values. 
 
=AVERAGE to calculate an 
average of the values in a 
range. That is, Excel totals  
 
Project-Based Learning 
Activity 
 
Review the symbols used in 
Excel that represent the 
standard mathematical 
operators:  
 
Multiply (*) asterisk 
 
Division / 
 
Addition + 
 
Subtraction – 
 
Use sample spreadsheet and 
demonstrate writing the 
formula to calculate values. 
 
Demonstrate the use of the 
SUM and AVERAGE 
Functions in calculating 
values/numbers 
 
 
 
Classwork: 
 
Students to use their sample 
Personal Budget sketch 
spreadsheets and to enter 
the data in a new worksheet 
or open the existing 
worksheet. 
 
Students to carryout 
calculations by writing the 
formula to add the totals.  
 
Students to use the SUM 
Function to add the totals. 
Then use the AVERAGE 
Function to get the average 
expense of their budget.  
 
 
Spreadsheets Are My 
Superpower: 
https://www.commonsense.
org/education/lesson-
plans/spreadsheets-are-my-
superpower

Objective 5.6.8: Create a simple chart with worksheet data 
 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
 
A chart is a graphic (picture) 
representation of data in a 
worksheet, Excel charts.  
 
A chart can be used as a 
descriptive way of 
representing the data; to 
clearly show trends or 
patterns in the data.  
 
Pie charts show the 
combination of each piece 
of data to the whole, or total 
of the data. 
 
Steps: 
 
 
A chart can be created 
by selecting the data 
from the worksheet, 
then select the type of 
chart to insert into the 
worksheet.  
 
 
Select the cell range (s) 
for the chart in the 
worksheet, then, on the 
Insert Tab, in the Charts 
group, click the chart 
type. (Pie) 
 
 
Save the chart with the 
worksheet. 
 
Project-Based Learning 
Activity 
 
Use Google-sheets simple 
pie chart templates for 
interactivity and 
demonstrations 
 
Provide students with the 
instructions from the 
selected activities. 
 
Students to follow and plot

Objective 6.1.1: Demonstrate proper use and care of devices and classroom rules.

Suggested Activities

Classroom Technology Rules 
 
 Only visit 
approved internet 
sites.  
 Never give out 
your personal 
information. 
 Leave your 
workspace as you 
found it!  
 Print only if you 
have permission. 
 Touch the mouse 
and keyboard 
gently. 
 Tell your teacher if 
you see something 
uncomfortable or 
inappropriate.  
 Never change 
settings without 
permission. 
 Never download 
anything without 
teacher 
permission. 
 Do NOT eat or 
drink near devices. 
 Place devices 
(Tablets, Laptops) 
on chargers when 
not in use.

How to Care for Various 
Digital Devices 
 
Laptops and Tablets 
 
Follow these steps to clean 
your laptop: 
 
Step One: Detach 
your battery, wipe 
it down with a dry 
cloth, and blow out 
the dust using a can 
of compressed air. 
 
Step Two: Wipe 
down the screen 
with the same cloth 
to remove any 
smudges. 
 
Cell Phones 
 
The best way to clean and 
disinfect your phone: 
 
Step One: Remove 
the phone from its 
case and turn the 
power off. 
 
Step Two: For a 
deeper clean, dip 
the corner of a soft 
cloth in isopropyl 
alcohol or white 
vinegar.  
 
Headphones and Ear Buds 
 
How to clean headphones: 
 
Step 1: Wash the 
foam or rubber 
pieces with 
isopropyl alcohol. 
Do not overly soak 
the towel you're 
using, but simply 
dab a corner into 
the rubbing 
alcohol. 
 
Step 2: Scrape  
 
Step 3: Dry 
thoroughly before 
using. 
 
Zoom 
 
Google Classroom 
 


 
Bahamas Ministry of Education Primary Computer Studies Curriculum Guide 
 
167
Go to Table of Contents 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
 
Game Consoles 
 
How to clean game consoles 
like Xbox: 
 
 
Step One:  Use a 
microfiber cloth for 
the outside  
 
Step Two:  Use 
compressed air to 
blow dust out of 
the vents.  
 
Step Three:  Use 
the compressed air 
to blow dust out of 
game cartridges 
and controller ports 
as well. 
 
Flash Drive 
 
How to clean your flash 
drive: 
 
 
Step One: Use 
rubbing alcohol and 
a Q-tip to clean 
your flash drive.  
 
Step Two:  Make 
sure it's completely 
dry before plugging 
it into the 
computer. 
 
Alexa, Google Home, 
Amazon Echo 
 
How to clean your Alexa, 
Google Home, or Amazon 
Echo: 
 
 
Step One:  Use a 
dry cloth to remove 
any dust that builds 
up on your voice 
assistant.  
 
Step Two:  Do not 
use any cleaners as 
moisture can easily 
damage your

device. 
 
Printers 
 
How to clean your printer: 
 
 
Step One:  Use 
rubbing alcohol, a 
clean cloth, and 
compressed air to 
wash it down.  
 
Step Two:  Avoid 
using paper towels 
as these can leave 
streaks.

assignments.

Objective 6.1.4: Describe digital citizenship and potential risks and dangers 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
 
Digital citizenship is the 
ability to safely and 
responsibly access digital 
technologies, as well as 
being an active and 
respectful member of 
society, both online and 
offline. 
 
Dangers Associated with 
Poor Digital Citizenship  
 
A lack of digital citizenship 
or poor digital citizenship 
can result in cyberbullying, 
irresponsible usage of social 
media, sharing sensitive 
personal details, and a lack 
of knowledge of Internet 
safety.

Objective 6.1.4: Define cyberbullying 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
 
Cyberbullying 
includes sending, posting, or 
sharing negative, harmful, 
false, or mean content 
about someone else. It can 
include sharing personal or 
private information about 
someone else causing 
embarrassment or 
humiliation. Some 
cyberbullying crosses the 
line into unlawful or criminal 
behavior.

Objective 6.1.5: List the effects of cyberbullying and strategies to prevent it 
 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
 
Negative Effects of 
Cyberbullying  
 
There are many detrimental 
outcomes associated with 
cyberbullying that reach 
into the real world. Many 
targets report feeling: 
 
 
Depressed 
 
Sad 
 
Angry 
 
Frustrated 
 
Low Self esteem 
 
Anxiety 
 
Family problems 
 
Academic 
difficulties 
 
School violence 
 
Suicidal 
thoughts/attempts 
 
How to Avoid Cyber Abuse 
 
 
Delete 
inappropriate 
photos 
 
Words have 
consequences. 
Be careful 
what you say 
to others 
online 
 
Don’t post 
anything mean 
online 
 
Don’t respond 
to a cyberbully 
 
Stand up for 
persons who 
are abused 
online 
 
Puzzles (Crossword, Word 
Search, Unscramble) 
 
Computer Vocabulary 
 
Role Play  
 
True and False Questions 
 
Appropriate 
presentation/videos

Students will play a 
Cyberbullying BINGO game 
 
Create a colorful, creative 
card to help stop 
cyberbullying 
 
Using Flip Grid share a video 
enacting the negative 
effects of cyberbullying. 
Include prevention 
strategies on how to avoid 
cyberbullying.

Objective 6.2.1a: Examine how computers have changed society. 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
  
A computer is an electronic 
device that manipulates 
information, or data. 
  
Computers come in many 
shapes and sizes, and they 
perform many different 
functions in our daily lives.  
  
Computers exist in many 
digital devices that we use 
on a day-to-day basis. 
  
  
When you withdraw cash 
from an ATM, scan groceries 
at the store, or use a 
calculator, you're using a 
type of computer. 
  
Desktop Computers 
Computers designed to be 
placed on a desk and used in 
that spot. They need a 
constant supply of 
electricity to function. 
  
 
 
 
Laptop Computers 
Battery-powered all-in-one 
computers that are more 
portable than desktops, 
allowing you to use them 
almost anywhere. 
  
 
Tablet Computers 
Handheld computers that 
are even more portable than 
laptops. 
  
Think-Pair-Share: Have 
students share with a 
partner their thoughts on 
what makes a device a 
computer. 
  
  
Have students watch the 
‘What is a Computer’ video. 
  
  
  
  
Have students complete a 
compare and contrast 
worksheet on the types of 
computers. 
 
  
  
  
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
Have students complete a 
Plickers activity to identify 
various digital devices. 
  
  
  
. 
  
  
 Share with students a video 
on ‘The Jetsons’ – the family 
of the future. Discuss which 
things are similar to what  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
Have students create an 
interactive timeline on the 
evolution of a chosen 
product with an embedded 
computer

Embedded Computers 
Many of today's electronics 
are basically specialized 
computers, though we don't 
always think of them that 
way. They are designed to 
complete one specific task. 
Like, smartphones, 
wearables, game consoles, 
smart TVs, washing 
machines, microwaves, and 
smart speakers.1

Objective 6.2.1b: Connect technology devices to their jobs. 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
  
The basic parts of a desktop 
computer are the system 
unit, monitor, keyboard, 
and mouse. 
  
Laptop computers have all 
their parts in one case – 
screen, keyboard, and 
touchpad. 
  
Instead of a keyboard and 
mouse, tablet computers 
use a touch-sensitive 
screen for typing and 
navigation.1 
  
While some of their external 
parts may be different, they 
all have similar internal 
components.  
  
Some internal components 
of a computer are: 
- central processing unit 
(CPU) 
- mother board  
- RAM 
- hard drive 
- Power supply 
- video card 
 
- sound card8

‘Hello Ruby: Journey Inside 
the Computer’.

and assemble an old digital 
devices, looking for and 
naming key components.

students share 
(verbally/written) one thing

things they learned from 
Ruby’s adventure.

computer parts to the tasks 
that are accomplished when 
they are used.

Objective 6.2.2: Classify hardware components. 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
  
A computer is made up of 
many parts that work 
together. 
  
The parts of the computer 
that can be seen and 
touched are called 
hardware.2 
  
Each hardware component 
has a specific job it does to 
help the digital device work. 
  
Five groups that hardware 
components can be divided 
into are: 
  
- Input Devices – used to 
enter data into the 
computer. Data can be 
letters, numbers, sounds, or 
images. Examples: mouse, 
keyboard, stylus, smart 
pencil, touchscreen, joystick, 
remote control, touchpad, 
scanner, digital camera, web 
camera, microphone, 
drawing tablet, and 
interactive whiteboard. 
  
- Output Devices – used to 
hear and see information 
from the computer. You use 
an output device to see or 
hear information from the 
computer. Information can 
be sound through speakers, 
art displayed on the screen, 
or text and graphics on a 
paper. Examples: monitor, 
screen, printer, speaker, 
headphones, and projector. 
  
Have students watch the 
video ‘Input, Output, and 
Storage Devices’ video. 
  
Have students complete the 
input/output/storage/proces
sing interactive worksheet. 
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
Have students complete a 
Mind Map classifying the 
hardware components with 
examples

Devices video:

watch?v=b7uwVe7M8Pg

Processing Interactive 
Worksheet:

- Storage Devices – used to 
save work to be retrieved 
later. Examples: flash drive, 
CD, DVD, hard drive, 
external hard drive, memory 
cards, and the cloud. 
  
- Processing Devices – reads 
the input and determines 
what it needs to do. 
  
- System Unit – protects the 
internal components of the 
computer, like the CPU, 
motherboard, and hard 
drive.2

Objective 6.2.3: Explain the IPO cycle. 
  
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
  
A computer helps us 
generate information from 
raw data.  
  
It follows the Input-
Process-Output (IPO) cycle: 
  
- We use an input device to 
enter data into a computer. 
This data is called the input. 
  
- The CPU converts the data 
into meaningful 
information. This is called 
processing.  
  
- During the processing, the 
data or information are 
stored in the computer’s 
memory 
  
- After the data is processed, 
the result is conveyed 
through an output device. 
This is the output.5 
  
Have students watch the 
‘How Does a Computer 
Work?’ video. 
  
  
Have students complete a 
Quizizz identifying the 
input, process, and output 
of various IPO cycles. 
[Whole Class/ Group/ 
Partner/Individual] 
 
 
Present students with a 
variety of IPO cycles and 
have them identify the 
activity at each stage. [Print 
or Digital Worksheet 
/Notebook] 
  
Have students create a 
slideshow explaining how 
the IPO cycle works. 
  
  
 
 
 
 
 
Have students create a 
digital diorama showing 
how the IPO cycle works. 
 
  
How Does a Computer Work 
video: 
https://youtu.be/3e0aN_pPh
ME 
  
IPO Cycle Quizizz: 
https://quizizz.com/admin/q
uiz/60ee7229fa248c001e16c
0ad 
  
Digital Diorama software: 
https://www.tinkercad.com/
teach

Objective 6.2.4a: Explain the purpose of software. 
   
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
  
Software are instructions 
that tell the computer what 
to do. There are two main 
types: system software and 
application software. 
  
System Software are the 
programs that run behind 
the scenes to ensure the 
computer functions 
properly, like the operating 
system and utility programs. 
  
An operating system is the 
most important software 
that runs on a computer. It 
manages the computer's 
memory and processes, as 
well as all its software and 
hardware. Without an 
operating system, a 
computer is useless.9 
  
Application Software are 
the programs used to 
perform specific computer 
tasks. 
  
  
They can be divided into 
two groups – general 
purpose and special 
purpose. 
  
 
General Purpose software to 
carry out lots of different 
tasks using that application. 
  
Special Purpose software 
perform one specific task 
like a flight simulator or 
  
Round Robin Question – 
What is software? 
  
 
Share with students the 
‘What is Software’ video. 
  
 
Share with students the 
‘Understanding Operating 
Systems’ video. 
  
 
Scavenger Hunt 
Use your Internet sleuthing 
skills to match the name of 
the operating system to its 
logo. 
  
 
 
Have students perform a 
digital research scavenger 
hunt to find examples of 
application software based 
on their uses. 
  
  
Using a T-Chart, have 
students sort general-
purpose and special- 
purpose software. 
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
Have students create a short 
video (Flipgrid) explaining 
the purpose of the different 
types of software.

Systems video:

Objective 6.2.4b: Discover contributions to software advancement by female pioneers. 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
  
Ada Lovelace is known as 
the first computer 
programmer. 
  
Rear Admiral Grace Hopper 
was one of the first people 
to work on/with the Harvard 
Mark 1. Her work was 
instrumental in the creation 
of the programming 
language COBOL. 
  
Hedy Lamarr, a Hollywood 
actress with a passion for 
science and engineering. 
Created a frequency-
hopping software that 
became the basis of 
bluetooth and wireless 
technology. 
 
 
  
Quick Write 
Name 5 female inventors 
and their inventions. Was it 
difficult to name these 
female inventors? If so, 
why? 
  
  
Have students watch videos 
on Ada Lovelace, Grace 
Hopper, and Hedy Lamarr. 
  
 
Journal Writing 
Have students share any 
ideas for inventions they 
have – whether it is 
something new or an 
improvement on a current 
device. 
 
 
Have students research and 
present on Katherine 
Johnson or other female 
computer pioneers. 
  
Have students compose an 
email to Ada Lovelace 
telling her all about how 
computers - and the 
programs that drive them - 
have changed the world. Be 
specific! Describe the 
advances in computer 
technology that have had 
the biggest impact on your 
life. Explain how they can be 
traced back to Lovelace's 
work, or her predictions for 
what computers might be 
able to do in the future.11 
  
 
For each computer 
innovation (Harvard Mark 1, 
UNIVAC 1, and COBOL), 
briefly describe its original 
purpose, Grace Hopper's 
contribution to its 
development, and its impact 
on modern computing. Can 
be presented in any format - 
slideshow, video recording, 
infographic, speech, 
paper).12

Objective 6.2.5a: Discuss the role of GUI. 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
  
The way an interface is 
designed, dictates its ease 
of use to the user. 
  
Modern operating systems 
use a graphical user 
interface, or GUI 
(pronounced gooey). A GUI 
lets you use your mouse to 
click icons, buttons, and 
menus, and everything is 
clearly displayed on the 
screen using a combination 
of graphics and text.9 
  
  
Have students view the 
‘Microwave Racing’ video.

of the various devices 
effected the task the user 
had to complete.

Content

Resources 
  
Pictures and words work 
together all the time. 
  
Many pictures in the real 
world give you information. 
Many of these pictures are 
symbols. 
  
Symbols are very simple 
pictures that tell you 
something, like which 
bathroom to use, where to 
throw your trash, or when 
something is not allowed. 
They are easily understood 
by people around the world. 
  
When you use technology, 
you will see even more 
symbols.6

Objective 6.2.6: Evaluate cloud computing and model its use. 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
  
The cloud (cloud computing 
or cloud storage) is the 
Internet - more specifically, 
it's all of the things you can 
access remotely over the 
Internet. When something is 
in the cloud, it means it's 
stored on Internet servers 
instead of your computer's 
hard drive. 
  
Two main reasons people 
use the cloud are 
convenience and reliability. 
They can store files, share 
files, back up data for future 
use.7 
  
Microsoft 365 is a cloud 
service that allows you to 
use different software and 
save your work in the cloud. 
 
  
Have students watch the 
‘What is a Cloud?’ video. 
  
  
Have students create a 
poster on cloud computing. 
  
 
Explore the Office365 
platform with students, 
highlighting the different 
applications [Whole 
Class/Group/Partner] 
  
 
 
Have students research and 
debate the pros and cons of 
cloud computing. 
 
 
Have students upload a file 
to a shared folder or class 
notebook.

Objective 6.5.3: Define and identify algorithms 
 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
  
An algorithm lists the steps 
needed to complete a task. 
Computer scientists use 
algorithms to plan out the 
steps they want a computer 
to follow.  
  
Programs are created to 
implement algorithms. 
  
Algorithms can be 
represented as pseudocode 
or a flowchart, and 
programming is the 
translation of these into a 
computer program.  
  
If an algorithm has been 
designed, the computer 
program will follow this 
algorithm, step-by-step, 
which will tell the computer 
exactly what it should do. 
  
Examples of algorithms in 
everyday life are: recipes, 
traffic lights, GPS, brushing 
your teeth, and planting a 
seed. 
  
  
  
Round Robin: What are 
algorithms? 
  
  
  
  
Have students view the 
‘Algorithms’ video. What are 
some of the algorithms they 
see in the day-to-day living? 
[Whole Class Discussion]  
  
  
Have students complete a 
Sudoku puzzle. The process 
of creating an “algorithm” 
to solve one of these puzzles 
lends itself nicely to 
computational thinking 
skills.  
  
  
Have students complete 
page 3 in the Act 2 
workbook by drawing a line 
from each step in the 
Algorithm to the matching 
code block. 
  
Have students develop an 
algorithm to solve an 
assigned problem using a 
specific set of commands 
and use peer review to 
critique the solution. 
[Peer Evaluation] 
  
  
Have students create a 
FlipGrid video as thought 
they were teaching 
someone about algorithms. 
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
GCF – Algorithms: 
https://edu.gcfglobal.org/en
/computer-
science/algorithms/1/

https://www.youtube.com/

Objective 6.5.4: Demonstrate knowledge of the Scratch interface  
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
  
Scratch is an environment 
where you can build 
algorithms by combining 
code blocks together. 
  
You can create interactive 
stories, animations, 
artwork, and games. 
  
There are three main 
sections of the Scratch 
interface. 
  
On the left-hand side we 
have tools to control or 
change our characters. The 
main way is through our 
code blocks.  
  
There are different types of 
block categories or ways to 
control our characters.  
  
We can also change the way 
our characters look under 
the “costumes” tab. 
 
We can also add sound 
under the “sounds” tab. 
  
 
 
In the middle we have our 
scripts area. This is where 
we put together code blocks 
to create our algorithms, or 
instructions, for our 
character.  
  
We “drag and drop” the code 
blocks we want to use.  
  
  
Have students view the 
‘Scratch Basics’ video. 
Discuss products that can be 
made in Scratch, and the 
method used. 
  
  
Open a New Project (click 
on “create” on the top left) 
and explain the different 
components of the Scratch 
Interface. Have students 
view the Exploring Scratch 
3.0 sheet of the student 
workbook as a reference. 
[Individual] 
  
 
 
 
 
 
Pair and Share: Have 
students share with a 
partner what they would like 
to create in Scratch. Have a 
few students share their 
thoughts with the class. 
[Partner] 
  
  
Have students log into their 
accounts and explore the 
interface. Introduce the 
menu options: My Stuff; My 
Class; Studio. [Individual] 
  
  
Have students access the 
Hello Mr. Scratch project 
and use the blocks available. 
[Individual/Partner] 
  
Have students complete a 
LiveWorksheet, Kahoot, or 
Quizizz identifying the parts 
of the Scratch interface.

Objective 6.5.5a: Describe conditions 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
  
Selections are a bit different 
than sequences. 
  
Instead of following a 
specific order of events, 
they ask a question in order 
to figure out which path to 
take next. 
  
These questions are known 
as conditional statements. 
They tell the program what 
to do in the event the rule 
cannot be followed. 
  
A rule is something that 
tells your program the 
direction to run. 
  
A condition is an exception 
to a rule. It tells your 
program to change. It can 
be a true or false statement 
  
A loop with conditions is a 
loop that continually checks 
if a condition is true. 
  
Sensing entails noticing (or 
identifying) when a specific 
condition is true. 
  
 
When the bell rings at the 
end of the school day, what 
do you do? [leave school, go 
home, go outside, go to after 
school activities]  
 
What would you do if the 
bell doesn’t ring? [stay in 
  
Have students view the 
‘Kodable Conditions’ video. 
Discuss. [Whole Class] 
  
  
 
 
 
 
 
Have students complete a 
vocabulary matching 
worksheet. [Individual] 
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
Have students write out an 
algorithm for what to do at 
a traffic light. Ensure that 
conditions are included. 
  
  
  
 
 
 
 
 
Have students complete 
page 1 in the ECforAll Act 2 
Unit 2 student workbook. 
[Whole 
Class/Partner/Individual]

https://youtu.be/dJYIRcsdH

class, not leave yet] The 
school bell is a condition 
that tells you to do the

In computer programming a 
condition is a statement

is true (it rings), you leave 
school. When the school bell

stay in school. There are

Objective 6.5.5b: Using loops with conditions 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
  
Loops with conditions use 3 
types of blocks in a script to 
control the actions of a 
sprite: a “forever” loop 
block, an “if then” 
conditional block, and a 
Sensing block.  
  
  
The “if then” condition is 
defined by using a Condition 
block with a blue Sensing 
block. The Sensing block 
tells the program to “sense” 
if the sprite is touching a 
color, touching another 
sprite, or if a key on the 
keyboard is pressed.20 
  
  
  
Have students complete 
page 2 in the ECforAll Act 2 
Unit 2 student workbook. 
[Teacher’s Guide, page 4) 
  
  
  
Pair and Share: Have 
students discuss different 
examples of conditions that 
are always true, never true, 
and conditions that change 
(that are sometimes true). 
  
  
Have students complete 
page 7 in student workbook 
(with guidance). 
  
  
Have students complete the 
Loops with Conditions – Ice 
Cream Truck project 
(student workbook page 8). 
  
  
  
Have students complete 
page 16 in ECforALL Act 2 
Unit 2 student workbook. 
  
  
  
Have groups complete the 
Twister Maze (Student 
Workbook, page 3; 
Teacher’s Guide, page 5). 
[Teacher Observation]

Objective 6.5.6: Design and build robots  
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
  
A robot is a mechanical 
device that can be 
programmed to follow a set 
of instructions. Robots have 
processing units, sensors to 
help them perceive things in 
the surrounding 
environment, and motors 
and actuators so that they 
can move. Robots may also 
have the added 
programmable functionality 
of lights, sounds or speech 
recognition.21 
  
  
  
Harold the Robot 
In this activity children 
simply give directions to a 
“robot” (teacher/student) 
and find out which 
instructions the robot is able 
to follow, and how their 
instructions are taken 
literally: 
 
 1. Place a small collection of 
blocks/similar objects on a 
desk. 
 2. One person (perhaps the 
teacher or other adult for a 
start) plays the role of 
Harold the Robot. Harold 
can only respond to 
particular commands. These 
 commands are not given to 
the  
children, and can be made 
up on the fly. 
 
 3. Have a child talk Harold 
through making a tower out 
of the blocks using 
instructions such as “Move 
your hand to the left”, “Pick 
up the block beside 
 your hand” and so on. If the 
child gives an instruction 
that is too complex or 
otherwise not in Harold’s 
vocabulary (e.g. “put the 
three blocks on top of each 
 other”) then Harold 
expresses confusions by 
shaking his head or burying 
his head in his hands. 
4. The task is completed 
when the tower is built. At 
  
Have students write out a 
code using sequences, 
events, and loops, to 
program ‘Harold the Robot’.  
  
  
  
  
  
  
Have students complete the 
Robotify course. 
[Observation] 
  
CS Unplugged Harold the 
Robot: 
https://classic.csunplugged.
org/documents/activities/co
mmunity-activities/harold-
the-
robot/haroldtherobot.pdf

Plans: https://robotify-
production-media.s3-eu-
west-

_resources/edu-
fundamentals/Fundamental
s+1+Lesson+Plans.pdf

children about which 
commands it would be

aloud ‘Emma Ren, Robot 
Engineer’. Discuss concepts 
and procedures mentioned 
in the story. 
 
 
Have students build a Lego 
robot. The goal here is to 
build a robot using Lego 
blocks from only verbal 
instructions. One student 
will have already built a 
robot and will be the 
"programmer." That student 
instructs the other student 
how to build the same robot 
without looking at the 
finished project.

Objective 6.3.1: Define term keyboarding and label the parts of the keyboard. 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
   
Keyboarding is the process 
of inputting text (type) into 
a keyboard by pressing keys 
on a keyboard.  A keyboard 
is an input device.  
 
A keyboard has letter keys, 
number keys and special 
keys.  The letters, numbers 
and symbols are called 
characters.  
 
You type letters, numbers, 
and symbols to create 
documents. 
 
You use a keyboard to work 
on the Internet, play some 
games, and when you use 
most software.  
 
There are many types of 
keyboards.  Some types 
include:   
 
QWERTY 
 
Dvorak 
 
Colemak 
 
UKQWERTY 
 
 
 
The most commonly used 
keyboard is 
the"Qwerty"keyboard.  It is 
named after the top row of 
letters on the keyboard and 
was invented in 1864. 
   
Watch videos of different 
shapes and types of 
keyboards. 
 
Explain the parts of the 
keyboards on different 
devices. 
 
Have students do research 
on the different types of 
keyboards. 
 
Label the keyboard and 
explain their various parts 
   
Label the keyboard  
Explain the various parts of 
the keyboard. 
 
Matching the keys with their 
functions. 
 
Label the keyboard and 
explain their various parts

keyboard multiple choice 
worksheet

Objective 6.3.2: Demonstrate proper keyboarding posture  
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
   
How you sit when you use a 
keyboard is important.  How 
you sit is called posture.  
Good posture is important 
because not sitting correctly 
can result in injuries to your 
body.  
 
You should sit up straight 
when you use the keyboard.  
You should face the 
computer screen.  Your 
arms should rest in front of 
you.  Your hands should be 
clean.  You should place 
your fingers gently on the 
keys.  
 
When typing your work area 
should be arranged as 
follows:  
 
Keyboard directly 
in front of chair; 
front edge of 
keyboard even with 
edge of desk  
 
Monitor placed for 
easy viewing  
 
Book at right of 
keyboard  
   
Students will demonstrate 
proper/correct posture. 
 
Collaborate and create short 
videos to demonstrate the 
Do’s and Don’ts of proper 
posture.   
 
Extension Activity 
Observe postures of others 
using computerized devices 
and create a video showing 
good and bad posture in 
use.  
 
 
 
 
 
   
Identify good and bad 
posture from pictures. 
 
Differentiation    
Identify good and bad 
posture from pictures using 
yes and no responses. 
 
Proper Keyboarding 
Techniques: 
https://www.youtube.com/
watch?v=ee9eIsUzEOM

Objective 6.3.3: Demonstrate correct finger placement and reach techniques  
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
 
Finger Placement 
 
When you use a keyboard:    
Curve your fingers 
upright over the 
home keys,   
 
Keep your wrists 
low but not 
touching the 
keyboard,   
 
Hold your forearms 
parallel to the slant 
of the keyboard,   
 
Keep your body 
erect, sitting back 
in the chair   
 
Keep your feet flat 
on the floor  
 
The keys on the middle row 
of the keyboard are called 
the home row keys.    
 
The home keys are 
a s d f for the left 
hand and j k l ; for 
the right hand  
 
 
When you are 
ready to keyboard, 
you rest your 
fingertips on the 
home row keys.  
 
When you type a 
character that is 
not typed with a 
   
Show video to demonstrate 
correct finger placement. 
  
Observe students placing 
fingers correctly on home 
row keys. 
 
Students will practice typing 
the characters from the 
home row keys without 
looking at the keyboard 
 
Students may use printed 
keyboard replicas to 
practice home row finger 
placing and practice. 
 
Teacher may call characters 
from the home row keys as 
student type. 
 
Touch type home row keys. 
 
Touch type simple words 
from the home row.
