Objective 6.3.4: Identify and use special keys 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
   
Backspace - Deletes a 
character to the left of the 
cursor 
 
Caps Lock – Capitalizes all 
letters. 
 
Delete – Deletes a character 
to the right of the cursor. 
 
Enter – Completes or enters 
a command.  Moves cursor 
down to the next line. 
 
Tab – Indents 
 
Esc - Short for Escape, Esc is 
a key found on the top-left 
corner of a computer 
keyboard. It allows the user 
to abort, cancel, or close an 
operation. 
   
The spacebar - the longest 
bar at the bottom of the 
keyboard.  
 
The Backspace Key - helps 
you to erase a mistake on 
your screen, just like you 
would use an eraser in your 
book.  
 
The Directional or Arrow 
Keys - help you to move the 
cursor up, down, left and 
right without erasing any of 
your work.  
 
Shift Keys - The keyboard 
has 2 shift keys. Hold down 
   
Watch appropriate video of 
special keys. 
 
 
Have students explain the 
functions of the special 
keys. 
 
 
Provide reinforcement 
activities. 
 
   
Identify the special keys on 
the keyboard  
 
Match the keys with their 
functions. 
 
Type lists of simple words 
using the special keys. 
 
Classwork 
 
Quiz 
   
Special Keys

watch?v=geKIJEghaqU 
 
Special Keys 
https://www.youtube.com/
watch?v=4XS1_j1XhCE

Resources 
the shift key on the left side 
when you want to type 
capital letters with your 
right hand. Hold down the 
shift key on the right side 
when you want to type 
capital letters with your left 
hand. You hold down the 
shift key then press a letter 
key to type a capital letter. 
 
Lower case letters are small 
letters (such as a, e, or t).  
These letters will be 
obtained by pressing the 
assigned key.  
   
Upper case are capital 
letters (such as A, E, or T). 
They are obtained by using 
the caps lock key or the shift 
keys.  To do this, hold down 
the shift key while pressing 
the letter to make it 
capitalized or press the Caps 
lock key which would also 
allow letters to also be 
typed in uppercase.  
  
When new keys are 
introduced, you are required 
to take your time in order to 
get used to the position of 
the keys.   
 
The movement to and from 
each key should be quick 
and a part of the act of 
striking.  
 
Return your fingers to the 
home keys immediately 
after striking the new keys.

Objective 6.3.6: Define term word processing 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
 
Word processing is the 
writing, manipulating, and 
storing of textual material 
on a computerized medium. 
   
Word Processing Software 
 
Microsoft Word 
 
Google Docs 
 
LibreOffice Writer 
 
OpenOffice Writer 
 
WPS Office Writer 
 
Word Pad 
 
WordStar 
Microsoft Word is one of the 
most popular and widely 
used word-processing 
software.   
   
   
   
   
   
   
   
   
   
   
   
 
Show examples of the 
different word processing 
software. 
 
Students will model 
accessing the MS Word. 
 
 
   
Identify the different word 
processing software. 
 
Match software names with 
their icons.

Objective 6.3.7a: Identify the features of the Word interface. 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
  
Some of the features of MS 
Word are as follows: 
 
Home:  font, size, font style, 
font color, bullets, line 
spacing, an alignment are 
some of the elements 
included on the home tab. 
 
Insert:  In your MS Word 
document, you can include 
graphs, shapes, images, 
charts, tables, footer, page 
number, and header, these 
may be found under the 
insert tab. 
 
Design:  Under the design 
tab you get a list of 
templates or design in which 
you want your document to 
be created to improve your 
documents appearance. 
 
Page Layout:  You get 
options like columns, lines, 
margins, orientation 
spacing, identification under 
the page layout tab. 
   
Open MS Word and explain 
the key features of a typical 
window. 
 
   
 Label the diagram of a MS 
Word window. 
 
Explain the features of the 
MS Word window.

features, shortcuts, uses, 
and other related questions

and-its-
features/articleshow/84464

Objective 6.3.7b: Enter and format text. 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
  
The Work Area 
 
After the Word window 
opens, there is a blank space 
for you to begin typing, 
similar to when you begin to 
write on a blank sheet of 
paper.  There is a blinking 
black line on the screen 
called the cursor.  This 
cursor indicates where the 
next character will be typed. 
 
 
Saving a Document 
 
It is very important to save 
your document in the event 
that you may wish to edit it 
or use it at a later date. 
 
Save your document as soon 
as you begin typing, and 
then save the changes about 
every five minutes as you 
type so you don’t lose your 
work. 
 
Step 1: Start a new 
document in Word and type 
your text. 
Step 2: Click File in the top 
left-hand corner of the 
screen. 
Step 3: From the menu, 
choose Save. 
Step 4: A ‘Save’ dialogue 
box will come up. At the top 
and at the left-hand side in 
the list of folder options, it 
will show the folder where 
you’ll be saving the 
   
Teacher would demonstrate 
the use of the following:  
 
add text 
 
enter text 
 
format text: font, 
style, size, and 
color 
 
adjust line spacing 
 
insert and format 
WordArt 
 
insert and format 
clip art or picture 
file 
 
modify the text 
wrap of an object 
 
draw and format 
shapes 
 
scale, move, and 
rotate objects 
 
insert a simple 
page border 
 
spell check a 
document 
 
print preview 
 
 
print a document 
 
cut, copy, and 
paste a selection 
 
copy formatting 
from a selection 
 
Use spell check 
features in simple 
documents. 
 
Name, save, open, and print 
simple documents. 
 
 
 
 
 
 
Create and format simple 
text documents using font, 
style, color, bold, italic, 
underline, alignment, select, 
cut, copy, and paste 
options.

worksheet 
https://www.liveworksheets
.com/md2049753ma

worksheet 
https://www.liveworksheets
.com/ri2528805sd

document. If you wish to 
change this folder, navigate 
through the folders on the 
left-hand side of the 
dialogue box to choose the

Step 5: Word will 
automatically give your 
document a name, based on 
the first few words of your 
text. If you don’t like the one 
given, type a name for your 
document in the ‘File name’

Step 6: Once you have

now have a name, which will 
be shown at the very top of

you make changes to your 
document and then save 
them after it have been 
saved originally, the 
dialogue box will not come 
up again. It will just save 
your changes without any 
visual notification being 
shown.  
 
Printing a Document 
 
Step 1:  Click the File tab.  
Step 2:  Click Print.  
Step 3:  Examine the print 
preview on the right side of 
the screen to ensure the 
document appears correct.  
Step 4:  Select the correct 
printer by clicking the 
Printer list arrow and 
selecting it from the list.  
Step 5:  Adjust the printer 
settings using the options 
below the printer, described 
in the following table.  
Step 6:  The document is 
sent to the printer.

'Word Printing’.

Objective 6.4.1: Define graphics and multimedia. 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
 
GRAPHICS 
Graphics are all around us.  
Our world is made up of 
colors, shapes and words.  
Graphics are drawings and 
pictures. 
 
Examples of graphics may 
be found on: 
 
product wrappers 
and packaging 
 
Story books and 
textbook covers 
 
t-shirts 
 
School bags 
 
Face painting 
Graphic designs creatively 
put together colors, shapes, 
and words to form 
meaningful and pleasing 
design. 
 
 
MULTIMEDIA 
 
Multi means more than one; 
many or multiple. 
 
Media is a means of 
conveying information. 
 
Multimedia is the 
presentation of information 
through text, audio, 
graphics, video, and 
animation.  
 
The basic elements of 
multimedia are:  
 
Text – Characters 
  
Identify and discuss the 
different types of graphics in 
surroundings and personal 
items 
 
Describe graphic designs 
created 
 
Research local graphic 
designers 
 
Watch appropriate videos 
 
Extension Activities 
 
Collaborate with Art 
Teacher to assist with 
graphic designs 
 
Collaborate with Junkanoo 
Artists  
 
Watch appropriate video 
 
Create a sign or poster 
adding text and graphics 
 
Create a short video with 
audio recording, video, and 
photo images 
  
Create a simple graphic 
design using shapes (a teddy 
bear, a house, a vehicle). 
 
Quiz- Multiple Choice, 
Matching, True/False 
 
  
MS Paint 
 
Desktop Publishing 
 
Photoshop 
 
Adobe Illustrator 
 
Canva

create word,

Graphics – are 
digital

Objective 6.4.2: Explain the use of presentation software   
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
   
A presentation lets you 
combine text, graphics, 
video, and sound on 
individual pages which are 
called slides.  Many slides 
are saved into one file.  This 
is called a presentation.  
Presentations are called 
slide shows. 
 
Presentation software 
enables users to present 
information, graphics, 
videos, etc. through 
slideshows in an attractive 
way. 
 
Popular presentation 
software include Prezi, 
Google Slides, Keynote, 
Slides, Slide Dog, Canva, 
and PowerPoint. 
   
Watch video introducing 
popular presentation 
software 
   
Using a Venn Diagram 
compare and contrast 
popular presentation 
software. Examples:  Prezi, 
Google Slides, Keynote, 
Slides, Slide Dog, and 
PowerPoint 
 
Multimedia Software

watch?v=v0gydDBj7Dk

Objective 6.4.3: Explain PowerPoint. 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
 
PowerPoint is one of many 
software designed for 
making electronic slides/ 
presentations. 
 
The PowerPoint application 
lets you combine text, 
graphics, video, and sound 
on individual pages which 
are called slides. This file is 
called a presentation.        
 
A new blank presentation 
opens each time you start 
PowerPoint. 
 
You can use many devices 
to help make and give a 
presentation.  
Presentations are also called 
slide shows 
NOTE:  The PowerPoint 
window, and the screen 
resolution may look 
different based on the 
device used. 
 
Other 
Multimedia/Presentation 
Programs include:   
 
Google Slides 
 
Prezi 
 
Canva 
 
Prezi 
 
Powtoon 
 
SlideShare 
 
Emaze 
 
Slidebean 
  
Explain the Backstage View 
and the template themes 
 
Demonstrate proper design 
guidelines to use 
PowerPoint to create, save 
and view slides. 
 
Explain the different slide 
layouts 
 
Research and use another 
Presentation software to 
present a slideshow. 
  
Produce a 3 slides 
presentation with text, 
pictures about an event. 
 
Format text using different 
fonts and colors for 
enhancements 
 
Add transition to the slide 
 
Display the slides using the 
slideshow feature 
  
PowerPoint Software 
 
Introduction to Microsoft

Objective 6.4.4: Identify the features of the PowerPoint interface 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
 
The PowerPoint window has 
many of the same elements 
as other Microsoft 
programs.  It has the same 
toolbar buttons and menus 
used to open, save, draw 
objects, cut, copy, paste, 
insert clipart, check spelling, 
preview, print, etc. 
 
The PowerPoint window 
also has many new features 
that you use to create, 
format and view slides. 
 
Office button – displays a 
drop-down menu for 
creating, opening, saving, 
and printing 
 
Title Bar – displays the 
filename and program 
 
Ribbon – displays tabs that 
organize program 
commands by groups. 
 
Command buttons – are 
displayed beneath the tabs.  
They are used to execute a 
command or to display a 
drop-down menu of 
command options 
 
 
Outline tab – used to create 
and view slides in an outline 
format, 
 
Slides tab – used to see a 
tiny version of each slide 
that have been created, 
  
Demonstrate and explain 
the features of the MS 
PowerPoint window. 
 
Labeling diagrams 
 
Watch appropriate video 
 
  
Label the features of the 
PowerPoint window 
diagram. 
 
Introducing the PowerPoint 
Window 
https://www.thetraininglady
.com/powerpoint-window/ 
 
Diagram of PowerPoint 
window.

dpress.com/2013/03/ppt_scr
een.png?w=300&h=210

ngpowerpoint/wp-

3/05/pptwindow2-
1024x664.png

called a thumb nail. 
 
Slide pane – contains the 
current slide. 
 
Placeholders – are boxes 
with dotted boarders that 
are part of most slide 
layouts.  These boxes hold 
title and body text or 
objects such as charts, 
tables, and pictures   
Placeholders used to add 
text, drawings, clipart, video 
and sound to a slide. 
 
Note pane – is located below 
the slide pane and is used to 
type reference notes and 
additional comments about 
the slide. 
 
Drawing toolbar - 
Automatically displayed at 
the bottom of the window 
above the status bar. 
 
Status bar – shows the 
number of the slide in the 
slide pane and the total 
number of slides in the 
presentation.

Objective 6.4.5: Name the various slide layouts 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
  
Slide Layouts are the pre-
formatted design of a slide 
in PowerPoint.  
 
These are:  
 
 Title slide – first and 
main slide, to 
introduce the topic 
and presenter. 
 Title and content 
slide  
 Two Content 
 Comparison 
 Title Only 
 
When you create a slide, you 
choose a layout.  The way 
objects are put on a slide is 
the layout. 
 
You need to decide on the 
layout of each new slide you 
insert  
  
Explain the use of each 
layout 
 
  
  
  
Different Types of Slide 
Layouts in PowerPoint

layout-in-powerpoint/

Objective 6.4.6: Create a title slide and format text   
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
 
Whenever you create a new 
slide, you’ll need to choose a 
slide layout. 
 
Slide layouts contain place 
holders.  Place holders are 
pre-made boxes on a slide 
that allow you to enter 
information into a slide by 
clicking. 
 
The title slide is the first 
slide of a presentation.  It 
usually contains a title and a 
subtitle. 
 
The title tells the main idea 
of the presentation.     
   
To create a title page: 
 
1. Open PowerPoint. 
You are presented 
with a title slide. 
2. Enter the 
Presentation title in 
the ‘Click to Add 
Title’ text 
box/placeholder.  
3. Type your subtitle 
in the Click to Add 
Subtitle text 
box/placeholder. 
 
 
 
   
   
   
   
   
   
   
   
   
Students will watch a video 
demonstrating how to 
create and format a title 
slide. 
 
Teacher will lead students in 
Creating a title slide 
inserting text and graphics. 
 
 
 
   
Create a PowerPoint 
Presentation 
 
 
Generate content for a 5-
slide presentation on

Objective 6.4.7: Insert and format new slides adding texts and graphics 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
 
To create a new slide: 
1. Choose the Home 
tab. 
2. Click the New Slide 
button 
 in 
the Slides group. 
The Office Theme 
dialog box appears 
and displays several 
layout templates. 
3. Click the layout you 
want. The layout 
appears in the Slide 
pane of the 
PowerPoint 
window. 
 
To add text: 
1. To add text, click 
inside the 
placeholder and 
type. 
2. To add an 
additional slide to 
your presentation, 
do one of the 
following: 
3. Right-click the slide 
layout. A menu 
appears. Click 
Layout and then 
click the layout you 
want. 
4. Choose the Home 
tab, click the New 
Slide button 
, and then 
choose the slide 
layout you want.

Objective 6.4.8: Add animation to text and graphics 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
   
To add an animation effect 
to a PowerPoint slide, follow 
the steps below. 
 
1. In a slide, highlight 
the text or image 
you want to 
animate. 
2. On the Ribbon click 
the Animations tab. 
3. On the Animations 
tab, in the 
Advanced 
Animation section, 
click the Add 
Animation option. 
4. Select the desired 
type of animation 
effect.  
 
You can select an Entrance, 
Emphasis, and Exit 
animation effect.  
 
You can also select a Motion 
Path effect, if you want to 
change the motion path of 
the animation. 
   
   
   
   
     
https://www.computerhope.
com/issues/pictures/powerp
oint-add-animation.jpg

Objective 6.4.9: Preview, save, print, and deliver a presentation 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
   
Navigating the Slide Show 
 
If you want to go to the next 
slide do one of the 
following: 
     Press the Right Arrow 
key. 
     Press the Enter key. 
     Press the Page Down key. 
     Left-click the slide. 
  
If you want to go to the 
previous slide do one of the 
following: 
     Press the Left Arrow key. 
     Press the Backspace key. 
     Press the Page Up key. 
 
To end the slide show and 
return to PowerPoint press 
the Esc key.

Objective 6.6.1: Explain the use of the Excel program 
 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
 
Microsoft Excel (or Excel) is 
a program used to record, 
analyze, present reports 
that need calculations, such 
as a grade sheet, and to 
create charts.   
 
A spreadsheet is a table of 
rectangular grid, consisting 
of cells (rows and columns), 
that holds the data, which 
includes texts and numbers. 
 
Spreadsheets are used in 
business for budgeting, 
financial reporting, etc. 
Spreadsheet can be used for 
personal budgeting, 
tracking expenses, or 
creating a list of personal 
items. 
 
The advantage of an 
electronic spreadsheet is 
that the content can be 
easily edited and updated to 
reflect changes in the 
calculated data. 
 
Project-Based Learning 
Activity 
 
PowerPoint presentations 
 
Watch appropriate videos 
 
Sample Expense 
Spreadsheet – School 
Supplies 
 
Sample Fast-Food-Fun 
Spreadsheet 
 
 
Provide a list with School 
Supplies. Students to enter 
data in spreadsheet 
 
Plan a Personal Expense 
Spreadsheet – listing items, 
costs, and calculate total. 
 
Save the data to use in 
creating a new excel 
worksheet.

Objective 6.6.2: Demonstrate opening and closing a workbook and a worksheet 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
 
To start Excel 
 
On the Windows taskbar, 
click the Start button to 
open the Start menu. 
 
On the Start menu, scroll 
through the list of apps, 
then click Excel. Excel will 
open in Backstage view. 
 
The Backstage view allows 
for the use of a blank 
workbook, open an existing 
workbook, or use a preset 
workbook called a template.  
 
The File tab on the Ribbon, 
shows various screens of 
commands that can be used 
to manage files and options 
in using Excel. 
 
TOUCH SCREEN DEVICES   
Point out the differences in 
the Office and windows 
interfaces. (Ribbon 
increases in height, buttons 
are bigger with more space 
around each, to move easily 
using the fingers or a stylus 
to tap the button.) 
 
Closing a Workbook  
On the ribbon, click the File 
tab to display the Backstage 
view, and then click Close in 
the navigation bar (or press 
CTRL + W) on the keyboard. 
 
A dialog box may appear,

Activity

View

workbook and worksheet.

program and worksheet on 
their device.

features of Backstage view

the interfaces of the various 
devices used. 
 
 
 
 
Students close the 
workbook and worksheet on 
their devices  
 
Students explain what 
happens after closing a 
worksheet and the 
workbook

Objective 6.6.3: Identify parts and features of a worksheet  
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
 
Open a new, blank 
workbook; The parts are: 
 
Title Bar -shows Book 1-
Excel, when a worksheet is 
saved the file name will be 
displayed in the Title bar. 
Ribbon Display Options: 
Minimize, Restore and 
Maximize buttons.  The 
organizing of the Ribbon 
into Tabs and the related 
Command buttons 
Name Box – shows the 
address of the active cell, 
Example A1 – this indicates 
the active cell is where 
column A and row 1 
intersect. Data is entered in 
the active cell. 
Insert Function – is used to 
choose and insert a built-in 
function. 
Active Cell – The current 
cell with the thick 
rectangular border (green) 
around the cell. 
Column Headings – 
Identified by the letters at  
the top of each column – 
Column name. 
Row Headings – The 
numbers along the left side 
of each row – the row 
number. 
Sheet Tabs – Shows the 
name of the current or 
active worksheet. Zoom 
Controls 
 
Scroll Bars – Used to move 
vertically or horizontally

Basic Terminology: 
An excel file is called a 
Workbook. A workbook 
contains one or more 
individual worksheets. 
Worksheet – contains grid, 
make up of rows and 
columns. 
Cell – A cell is the 
intersection of a row and a 
column. (Contain text, 
number or formula) Cell 
Range 
Label – Texts entry or data 
Values – Numeric values; 
default at right aligned 
Formulas – calculation 
commands that perform 
operations on the data. (Cell 
references, arithmetic 
operators, and 
functions.)22,23

Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s)

Moving around the cells of a 
worksheet using the 
following methods:  
 
Pointing and clicking in a 
cell (block plus sign cursor) 
Scroll Bars arrows;  
 
Directional Arrows or 
Cursor Control Keys (Left, 
Right, Up, Down); Home 
Key and CTRL + Home, End, 
CTRL +G or F5 (Go To dialog 
box to move quickly to a cell 
address. TAB Key; PGUP, 
PGDN.  
 
The horizontal and vertical 
scroll bars to move to other 
areas of the worksheet.

movements around the 
worksheet.

Objective 6.6.5: Create a blank worksheet or use a template to enter data  
 
 
 
 
 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
 
Create a new workbook 
from the new screen in 
Backstage view. Use the 
blank workbook template or 
open an existing one. 
 
Note: using the CTRL + N or 
a new blank document in 
any Office application. 
 
To enter data into a cell, it 
must be selected. The 
easiest way to select a cell 
(make it active) is to use the 
mouse to move the block 
plus sign pointer to the cell 
and click it. Use the Arrow 
Keys. When the cell is 
selected, the thick border 
surrounds the cell, and the 
active cell reference appears 
in the Name Box. The active 
cell column and row 
headings color changes to a 
darker shade. 
Enter data into a cell and 
pressing the Enter key, 
moving the cell cursor to the 
next cell in the column. 
 
Project-Based Learning 
Activity 
 
Presentation Video

enter texts, numbers and 
dates.

types and their 
position/alignment in a cell.

cells and to point out the 
active cell.

Personal Expense

and to enter the data in a 
new worksheet.

assigned tasks.

Objective 6.6.6: Format, save, and print a worksheet  
 
 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
 
Formatting enhances the 
appearance of the 
worksheet data by changing 
font, size, color, alignment, 
and adding borders. Borders 
are useful when a worksheet 
is printed, to show the 
gridlines 
 
Saving a worksheet – This is 
done to keep the document 
for later use or to share with 
others. Using the Backstage 
view – File – Save or Save 
As. From the Keyboard: Ctrl 
+S in all Office Program. 
 
Printing is necessary for a 
paper-based copy of the 
worksheet. From the File – 
Backstage View. Excel has 
many tools to control the 
print layout and appearance 
of a worksheet. Preview 
before printing for 
correctness. 
 
Project-Based Learning 
Activity 
 
Presentation Videos

worksheet. 
 
Demonstrate the uses of the 
Save/Save As commands 
and print options.

worksheet: -

data, perform calculations, 
format, save, preview, and 
print a hard copy or Screen 
Share

the Blanks

Objective 6.6.7: Perform simple calculation using formula and the SUM function 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
 
A formula is a calculation 
using numbers in a cell. 
Using a formula to calculate 
values allow you to focus on 
the data and allow Excel to 
automatically recalculate 
the results, if the data has to 
be changes. 
 
To begin a formula in any 
cell, it must begin with the 
equal (=) sign/symbol. Then 
a cell address, a 
mathematical operator, 
then another cell address. 
Example: = B2+C3 
 
Enter a cell address into a 
formula by typing it directly 
into the cell. By clicking on 
the cell to be included. The 
cell into which you enter a 
formula will display the 
result. 
  
Note: the formula will be 
seen in the formula Bar. 
 
Introduce Common Built-In 
Functions 
 
A function is pre-set 
operator in Excel to accept 
the values/numbers, and cell 
references when selected 
for calculations. 
 
Examples: =SUM to add the 
total of the values. 
 
=AVERAGE to calculate an 
average of the values in a 
range. That is, Excel totals 
 
Project-Based Learning 
Activity 
 
Review the symbols used in 
Excel that represent the 
standard mathematical 
operators:  
 
Multiply (*) asterisk 
 
Division / 
 
Addition + 
 
Subtraction – 
 
Use sample spreadsheet and 
demonstrate writing the 
formula to calculate values. 
 
 
 
 
 
 
Demonstrate the use of the 
SUM and AVERAGE 
Functions in calculating 
values/numbers 
 
 
Students to use their sample 
Personal Expense 
spreadsheets and to enter 
the data in a new worksheet 
or open the existing 
worksheet. 
 
Students to carryout 
calculations by writing the 
formula to add the totals.  
 
Students to use the SUM 
Function to add the totals.  
 
Use the AVERAGE Function 
to get the average expense 
for their budget.  
 
Spreadsheets Are My 
Superpower: 
https://www.commonsense.
org/education/lesson-
plans/spreadsheets-are-my-
superpower

Objective 6.6.8: Create simple pie and column charts with worksheet data  
 
 
Content 
Suggested Activities 
Suggested Assessment(s) 
Resources 
 
A chart is a graphic (picture) 
representation of data in a 
worksheet, Excel charts.  
 
A chart can be used as a 
descriptive way of 
representing the data; to 
clearly show trends or 
patterns in the data.  
 
Pie charts show the 
combination of each piece 
of data to the whole, or total 
of the data. A column 
(vertical presentation) or 
bar chart (horizontal 
presentation) is used to 
show comparison or 
ranking. 
 
Steps: 
 
 
A chart can be created 
by selecting the data 
from the worksheet, 
then select the type of 
chart to insert into the 
worksheet.  
 
 
Select the cell range (s) 
for the chart in the 
worksheet, then, on the 
Insert Tab, in the Charts 
group, click the chart 
type. (Pie/Column) 
 
 
Save the chart with the 
worksheet. 
 
Project-Based Learning 
Activity 
 
Use Google-sheets simple 
pie chart templates for 
interactivity and 
demonstrations, any other 
suitable application 
 
Provide students with the 
instructions from the 
selected activities. 
 
Students to follow and plot 
the Pie chart; explain each 
step and parts 
 
Students to follow creating 
a column or bar chart using 
the same data. 
 
 
 
Demonstrate the default 
standard layouts – Adding 
chart elements. 
 
Projects: 
 
Kyla’s M & M Pie Chart. 
 
Budget Pie Chart 
 
Ari’s Fruits Pie Chart 
 
Have students plot Column 
Charts using the data. 
 
Provide other suitable 
exercises as necessary 
 
Test/Quiz: 
 Multiple choice 
 True/False 
 Matching 
 Fill-in the Blanks

watch?v=0Go7I7cz0Ig
